<li><i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man:_Far_From_Home" title="Spider-Man: Far From Home">Spider-Man: Far From Home</a></i> (2019)</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="In_music_videos">In music videos</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: In music videos">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The city has been the setting for music videos of such songs as <a href="/wiki/Siouxsie_and_the_Banshees" title="Siouxsie and the Banshees">Siouxsie and the Banshees</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Dear_Prudence#Cover_versions" title="Dear Prudence">Dear Prudence</a>"  in 1983 and <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Like_a_Virgin_(song)" title="Like a Virgin (song)">Like a Virgin</a>" in 1984.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="In_video_games">In video games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: In video games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The city is the setting for parts of such video games as <i><a href="/wiki/Assassin%27s_Creed_II" title="Assassin&#39;s Creed II">Assassin's Creed II</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Tomb_Raider_II" title="Tomb Raider II">Tomb Raider II</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> It has also served as inspiration for the fictional city of Altissia, in <i><a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XV" title="Final Fantasy XV">Final Fantasy XV</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> The city also serves as a setting for <i><a href="/wiki/The_House_of_the_Dead_2" title="The House of the Dead 2">The House of the Dead 2</a></i>. The city appears as the first main level in <i><a href="/wiki/Sly_3:_Honor_Among_Thieves" title="Sly 3: Honor Among Thieves">Sly 3: Honor Among Thieves</a></i>. It is also featured in <a href="/wiki/Valve_Corporation" title="Valve Corporation">Valve's</a> first-person shooter <i><a href="/wiki/Counter-Strike:_Global_Offensive" title="Counter-Strike: Global Offensive">Counter-Strike: Global Offensive</a></i> as the inspiration for the multiplayer map "Canals".
</p><p>Venice was the base theme for Soleanna, one of the hub worlds in <i><a href="/wiki/Sonic_the_Hedgehog_(2006_video_game)" title="Sonic the Hedgehog (2006 video game)">Sonic the Hedgehog</a></i>. One of the nine playable characters, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Sonic_the_Hedgehog_characters#Silver_the_Hedgehog" title="List of Sonic the Hedgehog characters">Silver the Hedgehog</a>, was once a <a href="/wiki/Mink" title="Mink">mink</a> named "Venice" during development. The idea was ultimately scrapped.
</p><p>In April 2018, <i><a href="/wiki/Overwatch_(video_game)" title="Overwatch (video game)">Overwatch</a></i> released the map Rialto, based on the city center.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Photography">Photography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Photography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Photograph_of_Guardi%27s_Regatta_in_Venice_at_the_Frick_Art_Reference_Library.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Photograph_of_Guardi%27s_Regatta_in_Venice_at_the_Frick_Art_Reference_Library.jpg/220px-Photograph_of_Guardi%27s_Regatta_in_Venice_at_the_Frick_Art_Reference_Library.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Photograph_of_Guardi%27s_Regatta_in_Venice_at_the_Frick_Art_Reference_Library.jpg/330px-Photograph_of_Guardi%27s_Regatta_in_Venice_at_the_Frick_Art_Reference_Library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Photograph_of_Guardi%27s_Regatta_in_Venice_at_the_Frick_Art_Reference_Library.jpg/440px-Photograph_of_Guardi%27s_Regatta_in_Venice_at_the_Frick_Art_Reference_Library.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2744" data-file-height="1705" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Photograph_of_Guardi%27s_Regatta_in_Venice_at_the_Frick_Art_Reference_Library.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Photograph of Guardi's Regatta in Venice at the Frick Art Reference Library.</div></div></div>
<p>Its splendid architecture, artworks, landscapes, <a href="/wiki/Gondolas" class="mw-redirect" title="Gondolas">gondolas</a>, the alternance of high and low tides, the reflections of light and colors, and the unusual daily scenes in a city living on water, make of Venice and its islands a paradise for photographers both professional and amateur. <a href="/wiki/Fulvio_Roiter" title="Fulvio Roiter">Fulvio Roiter</a> has probably been the pioneer in artistic photography in Venice,<sup id="cite_ref-auto_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> followed by a number of photographers whose works are often reproduced on postcards, thus reaching a widest international popular exposure.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Venetian_cuisine" title="Venetian cuisine">Venetian cuisine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Veneto_wine" class="mw-redirect" title="Veneto wine">Veneto wine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ca%27_Rezzonico_-_La_cioccolata_del_mattino_-_Pietro_Longhi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Ca%27_Rezzonico_-_La_cioccolata_del_mattino_-_Pietro_Longhi.jpg/170px-Ca%27_Rezzonico_-_La_cioccolata_del_mattino_-_Pietro_Longhi.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Ca%27_Rezzonico_-_La_cioccolata_del_mattino_-_Pietro_Longhi.jpg/255px-Ca%27_Rezzonico_-_La_cioccolata_del_mattino_-_Pietro_Longhi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Ca%27_Rezzonico_-_La_cioccolata_del_mattino_-_Pietro_Longhi.jpg/340px-Ca%27_Rezzonico_-_La_cioccolata_del_mattino_-_Pietro_Longhi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3203" data-file-height="4269" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ca%27_Rezzonico_-_La_cioccolata_del_mattino_-_Pietro_Longhi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hot chocolate was a fashionable drink in Venice during the 1770s and 1780s.</div></div></div>
<p>Venetian cuisine is characterized by seafood, but also includes garden products from the islands of the lagoon, rice from the mainland, game, and <a href="/wiki/Polenta" title="Polenta">polenta</a>. Venice is not known for a peculiar cuisine of its own: it combines local traditions with influences stemming from age-old contacts with distant countries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> These include <i>sarde in saór</i> (sardines marinated to preserve them for long voyages); <i>bacalà mantecato</i> (a recipe based on Norwegian <a href="/wiki/Stockfish" title="Stockfish">stockfish</a> and extra-virgin olive oil); <i>bisàto</i> (marinated eel); <i>risi e bisi</i> – rice, peas and (unsmoked) bacon;<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> <i>fegato alla veneziana</i>, Venetian-style veal liver; <i>risòto col néro de sépe</i> (risotto with cuttlefish, blackened by their own ink); <i>cichéti</i>, refined and delicious tidbits (akin to <i>tapas</i>); <i>antipasti</i> (appetizers); and <i><a href="/wiki/Prosecco" title="Prosecco">prosecco</a></i>, an effervescent, mildly sweet wine.
</p><p>In addition, Venice is known for the golden, oval-shaped cookies called <i><a href="/wiki/Baicoli" title="Baicoli">baìcoli</a></i>, and for other types of sweets, such as: <i>pan del pescaór</i> (bread of the fisherman); cookies with almonds and pistachio nuts; cookies with fried Venetian cream, or the <i>bussolài</i> (<a href="/wiki/Butter_biscuit" class="mw-redirect" title="Butter biscuit">butter biscuits</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shortbread" title="Shortbread">shortbread</a> made in the shape of a ring or an "S") from the island of Burano; the <i>galàni</i> or <i>cróstoli</i> (<a href="/wiki/Angel_wings" title="Angel wings">angel wings</a>);<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> the <i>frìtole</i> (fried spherical doughnuts); the <i>fregolòtta</i> (a crumbly cake with almonds); a milk pudding called <i>rosàda</i>; and cookies called <i>zaléti</i>, whose ingredients include yellow maize flour.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The dessert <a href="/wiki/Tiramisu" title="Tiramisu">tiramisù</a> is generally thought to have been invented in <a href="/wiki/Treviso" title="Treviso">Treviso</a> in the 1970s,<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> and is popular in the <a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">Veneto</a> area.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion_and_shopping">Fashion and shopping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Fashion and shopping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luxury_shops_and_boutiques_along_the_Rialto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Luxury_shops_and_boutiques_along_the_Rialto.jpg/170px-Luxury_shops_and_boutiques_along_the_Rialto.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Luxury_shops_and_boutiques_along_the_Rialto.jpg/255px-Luxury_shops_and_boutiques_along_the_Rialto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Luxury_shops_and_boutiques_along_the_Rialto.jpg/340px-Luxury_shops_and_boutiques_along_the_Rialto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2736" data-file-height="3648" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luxury_shops_and_boutiques_along_the_Rialto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Luxury shops and boutiques along the <a href="/wiki/Rialto_Bridge" title="Rialto Bridge">Rialto Bridge</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In the 14th century, many young Venetian men began wearing tight-fitting multicoloured hose, the designs on which indicated the <i>Compagnie della Calza</i> ("Trouser Club") to which they belonged. The Venetian Senate passed <a href="/wiki/Sumptuary_law" title="Sumptuary law">sumptuary laws</a>, but these merely resulted in changes in fashion in order to circumvent the law. Dull garments were worn over colourful ones, which then were cut to show the hidden colours resulting in the spread of men's "slashed" fashions in the 15th century.
</p><p>Today, Venice is a major fashion and shopping centre; not as important as <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a>, and Rome, but on a par with <a href="/wiki/Verona" title="Verona">Verona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicenza" title="Vicenza">Vicenza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>. <a href="/wiki/Roberta_di_Camerino" class="mw-redirect" title="Roberta di Camerino">Roberta di Camerino</a> is the only major <a href="/wiki/Italian_fashion" title="Italian fashion">Italian fashion</a> brand to be based in Venice.<sup id="cite_ref-josh_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-josh-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Founded in 1945, it is renowned for its innovative handbags featuring hardware<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> by Venetian artisans and often covered in locally woven velvet, and has been credited with creating the concept of the easily recognisable <a href="/wiki/It_bag" title="It bag">status bag</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-josh_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-josh-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Many of the fashion boutiques and jewelry shops in the city are located on or near the <a href="/wiki/Rialto_Bridge" title="Rialto Bridge">Rialto Bridge</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/Piazza_San_Marco" title="Piazza San Marco">Piazza San Marco</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In January 2000, the City of Venice and the Central Association of Cities and Communities of Greece (KEDKE) established, in pursuance to <a href="/wiki/Regulation_(European_Union)" title="Regulation (European Union)">EC Regulation</a> No. 2137/85, the Marco Polo System <a href="/wiki/European_economic_interest_grouping" title="European economic interest grouping">European Economic Interest Grouping</a> (E.E.I.G.), to promote and realise European projects within transnational cultural and tourist fields, particularly in reference to the preservation and safeguarding of artistic and architectural heritage.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Twin towns and sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Italy" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Italy">List of twin towns and sister cities in Italy</a></div>
<p>Venice is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a>, Armenia, since 2011<sup id="cite_ref-Yerevan_twinnings_2_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yerevan_twinnings_2-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dubrovnik" title="Dubrovnik">Dubrovnik</a>, Croatia, since 2012<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Monter%C3%ADa" title="Montería">Montería</a>, Colombia, since 2018</li></ul>
<p>In 2013, Venice ended the sister city relationship with St. Petersburg in opposition to laws Russia had passed against homosexuals and those who support gay rights.<sup id="cite_ref-Venice_Russia_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Venice_Russia-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cooperation_agreements">Cooperation agreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Cooperation agreements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Venice has cooperation agreements with the Greek city of <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>; the German city of <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a>, signed on 25 September 1999; and the Turkish city of <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, signed on 4 March 1993, within the framework of the 1991 Istanbul Declaration. It is also a Science and Technology Partnership City with <a href="/wiki/Qingdao" title="Qingdao">Qingdao</a>, China.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Places_named_after_Venice">Places named after Venice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Places named after Venice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The name "<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Venezuela" class="extiw" title="wikt:Venezuela">Venezuela</a>" is a Spanish diminutive of Venice (<i>Veneziola</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><br />Many additional places around the world are named after Venice: e.g.
</p>
<dl><dd><a href="/wiki/Venice,_Los_Angeles" title="Venice, Los Angeles">Venice, Los Angeles</a>, home of Venice Beach</dd>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Venice,_Alberta" title="Venice, Alberta">Venice, Alberta</a>, in Canada</dd>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Venice,_Florida" title="Venice, Florida">Venice, Florida</a>, city in Sarasota County</dd>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Venice,_New_York" title="Venice, New York">Venice, New York</a></dd></dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ritratto_del_Doge_Andrea_Gritti_-_Tiziano_059.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Ritratto_del_Doge_Andrea_Gritti_-_Tiziano_059.jpg/170px-Ritratto_del_Doge_Andrea_Gritti_-_Tiziano_059.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Ritratto_del_Doge_Andrea_Gritti_-_Tiziano_059.jpg/255px-Ritratto_del_Doge_Andrea_Gritti_-_Tiziano_059.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Ritratto_del_Doge_Andrea_Gritti_-_Tiziano_059.jpg/340px-Ritratto_del_Doge_Andrea_Gritti_-_Tiziano_059.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8453" data-file-height="10934" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ritratto_del_Doge_Andrea_Gritti_-_Tiziano_059.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Doge <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Gritti" title="Andrea Gritti">Andrea Gritti</a>, reigned 1523–1538, portrait by <a href="/wiki/Titian" title="Titian">Titian</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Monument_to_Carlo_Goldoni_(Venice).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Monument_to_Carlo_Goldoni_%28Venice%29.jpg/170px-Monument_to_Carlo_Goldoni_%28Venice%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Monument_to_Carlo_Goldoni_%28Venice%29.jpg/255px-Monument_to_Carlo_Goldoni_%28Venice%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Monument_to_Carlo_Goldoni_%28Venice%29.jpg/340px-Monument_to_Carlo_Goldoni_%28Venice%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4987" data-file-height="7541" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Monument_to_Carlo_Goldoni_(Venice).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Carlo_Goldoni" title="Carlo Goldoni">Carlo Goldoni</a>, the most notable name in Italian theatre.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sebastian_Cabot_-_S._Rawle_after_Hans_Holbein,_1824.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Sebastian_Cabot_-_S._Rawle_after_Hans_Holbein%2C_1824.jpeg/170px-Sebastian_Cabot_-_S._Rawle_after_Hans_Holbein%2C_1824.jpeg" decoding="async" width="170" height="246" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Sebastian_Cabot_-_S._Rawle_after_Hans_Holbein%2C_1824.jpeg/255px-Sebastian_Cabot_-_S._Rawle_after_Hans_Holbein%2C_1824.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Sebastian_Cabot_-_S._Rawle_after_Hans_Holbein%2C_1824.jpeg/340px-Sebastian_Cabot_-_S._Rawle_after_Hans_Holbein%2C_1824.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="414" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sebastian_Cabot_-_S._Rawle_after_Hans_Holbein,_1824.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The explorer <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Cabot_(explorer)" title="Sebastian Cabot (explorer)">Sebastian Cabot</a>.</div></div></div>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Venice%22">"Venice"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Venice%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Venice%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Venice%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Venice%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Venice%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Others closely associated with the city include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Pietro_Cesare_Alberti" title="Pietro Cesare Alberti">Pietro Cesare Alberti</a> (1608–1655), considered the first Italian-American, arriving in New Amsterdam in 1635.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tomaso_Albinoni" title="Tomaso Albinoni">Tomaso Albinoni</a> (8 June 1671 – 17 January 1751), a <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">baroque</a> composer.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Claudio_Ambrosini" title="Claudio Ambrosini">Claudio Ambrosini</a> (9 April 1948), composer and conductor.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pietro_Bembo" title="Pietro Bembo">Pietro Bembo</a> (20 May 1470 – 18 January 1547), <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Cardinal" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic Cardinal">cardinal</a> and scholar.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Bellini" title="Giovanni Bellini">Giovanni Bellini</a> (<i>c.</i> 1430–1516), Renaissance painter, probably the best known of the Bellini family of painters.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Francesco_Borgato" title="Francesco Borgato">Francesco Borgato</a> (5 September 1990, Venice), Italian recording artist and dancer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marco_Antonio_Bragadin" title="Marco Antonio Bragadin">Marco Antonio Bragadin</a> (d. 1571), general, flayed alive by the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Turks</a> after a fierce resistance during the siege of <a href="/wiki/Famagusta" title="Famagusta">Famagusta</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Cabot_(explorer)" title="Sebastian Cabot (explorer)">Sebastian Cabot</a> (<i>c.</i> 1484–1557, or soon after), <a href="/wiki/List_of_explorers" title="List of explorers">explorer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Canaletto" title="Canaletto">Canaletto</a> (28 October 1697 – 19 April 1768), known for his landscapes or <i><a href="/wiki/Veduta" title="Veduta">vedute</a></i> of Venice, but not only.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rosalba_Carriera" title="Rosalba Carriera">Rosalba Carriera</a> (7 October 1675 – 15 April 1757), known for her pastel works.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Casanova" title="Giacomo Casanova">Giacomo Casanova</a> (1725–1798 in Dux, <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Duchcov" title="Duchcov">Duchcov</a>, Czech Republic)), a Venetian adventurer, writer and <a href="/wiki/Womanizing" class="mw-redirect" title="Womanizing">womanizer</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Francesco_Cavalli" title="Francesco Cavalli">Francesco Cavalli</a> (14 February 1602 – 14 January 1676), a <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">baroque</a> composer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Enrico_Dandolo" title="Enrico Dandolo">Enrico Dandolo</a> (<i>c.</i> 1107–1205), <a href="/wiki/Doge_of_Venice" title="Doge of Venice">Doge of Venice</a> from 1192 to his death, played a direct role in the <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Constantinople" title="Sack of Constantinople">Sack of Constantinople</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Crusade" title="Fourth Crusade">Fourth Crusade</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vincenzo_Dandolo" title="Vincenzo Dandolo">Vincenzo Dandolo</a> (1758–1819), chemist, agronomist and politician of the <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_Era" class="mw-redirect" title="Enlightenment Era">Enlightenment Era</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Da_Ponte" title="Lorenzo Da Ponte">Lorenzo Da Ponte</a> (1749–1838), opera librettist and poet, wrote the librettos for 28 operas by 11 composers, including <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ludovico_de_Luigi" title="Ludovico de Luigi">Ludovico de Luigi</a> (born 11 November 1933), Venetian Surrealistic artist.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dominic_DeNucci" title="Dominic DeNucci">Dominic DeNucci</a> (born 23 January 1932 as <i>Dominic Nucciarone</i>), Italian-American professional wrestler.</li>
<li>Pellegrino Ernetti (1925–1994), Catholic priest and exorcist, alleged constructor of the <a href="/wiki/Chronovisor" title="Chronovisor">chronovisor</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Veronica_Franco" title="Veronica Franco">Veronica Franco</a> (1546–1591), poet and courtesan during the Renaissance.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andrea_Gabrieli" title="Andrea Gabrieli">Andrea Gabrieli</a> (<i>c.</i> 1510–1586), Italian composer and organist at St Mark's Basilica.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Gabrieli" title="Giovanni Gabrieli">Giovanni Gabrieli</a> (1554/1557–1612), composer and organist at St Mark's Basilica.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carlo_Goldoni" title="Carlo Goldoni">Carlo Goldoni</a> (25 February 1707 – 6 February 1793). Along with <a href="/wiki/Pirandello" title="Pirandello">Pirandello</a>, Goldoni is probably the most notable name in Italian theatre, in his country and abroad.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carlo_Gozzi" title="Carlo Gozzi">Carlo Gozzi</a> (13 December 1720 – 4 April 1806), dramatist of the 18th century.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pietro_Guarneri" title="Pietro Guarneri">Pietro Guarneri</a> (14 April 1695 – 7 April 1762), left Cremona in 1718, settled in Venice. "Peter of Venice" from the family of great luthiers.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Baldassare_Longhena" title="Baldassare Longhena">Baldassare Longhena</a> (1598 – 18 February 1682), one of the greatest exponents of Baroque architecture.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Lotto" title="Lorenzo Lotto">Lorenzo Lotto</a> (<i>c.</i> 1480–1556), painter, draughtsman, and illustrator, traditionally placed in the <a href="/wiki/Venetian_School_(art)" class="mw-redirect" title="Venetian School (art)">Venetian school</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bruno_Maderna" title="Bruno Maderna">Bruno Maderna</a> (21 April 1920 – 13 November 1973), an Italian-German orchestra director and 20th-century music composer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aldus_Manutius" title="Aldus Manutius">Aldus Manutius</a> (1449–1515), one of the most important printers in history.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leon_Modena" class="mw-redirect" title="Leon Modena">Leon Modena</a> (1571–1648) preacher, author, poet, active in the Venetian ghetto and beyond.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Domenico_Montagnana" title="Domenico Montagnana">Domenico Montagnana</a> (24 June 1686 – 6 March 1750) was an Italian master <a href="/wiki/Luthier" title="Luthier">luthier</a>. He is regarded as one of the world's finest <a href="/wiki/Violin" title="Violin">violin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cello" title="Cello">cello</a> makers of his time.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Claudio_Monteverdi" title="Claudio Monteverdi">Claudio Monteverdi</a> (1567–1643), composer, opera pioneer, and director of music at <a href="/wiki/San_Marco" title="San Marco">San Marco</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Luigi_Nono_(composer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Luigi Nono (composer)">Luigi Nono</a> (29 January 1924 – 8 May 1990), a leading composer of instrumental and electronic music.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Pardo_(rabbi)" title="Joseph Pardo (rabbi)">Joseph Pardo</a> (<i>c.</i> 1561–1619), rabbi and merchant.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elena_Lucrezia_Cornaro_Piscopia" class="mw-redirect" title="Elena Lucrezia Cornaro Piscopia">Elena Lucrezia Cornaro Piscopia</a> (5 June 1646 – 26 July 1684), the first woman in the world to receive a doctorate degree.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a> (<i>c.</i> 1254 – 8 January 1324), trader and <a href="/wiki/Exploration" title="Exploration">explorer</a>, one of the first Westerners to travel the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> to China. While a prisoner in Genoa, he dictated in the tale of his travels known as <i>Il Milione</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Travels_of_Marco_Polo" title="The Travels of Marco Polo">The Travels of Marco Polo</a></i>).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Virgilio_Ranzato" title="Virgilio Ranzato">Virgilio Ranzato</a> (7 May 1883 – 20 April 1937), composer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Rolfe" title="Frederick Rolfe">Frederick Rolfe</a> (22 July 1860 – 25 October 1913), English author of the Venetian novel <i>The Desire and Pursuit of the Whole</i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carlo_Scarpa" title="Carlo Scarpa">Carlo Scarpa</a> (2 June 1906 – 28 November 1978, <a href="/wiki/Sendai,_Miyagi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sendai, Miyagi">Sendai, Japan</a>), an architect with a profound understanding of materials.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Romano_Scarpa" title="Romano Scarpa">Romano Scarpa</a> (27 September 1927 –23 April 2005), was one of the most noted Italian creators of Disney comics.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Sinopoli" title="Giuseppe Sinopoli">Giuseppe Sinopoli</a> (2 November 1946 – 20 April 2001), conductor and composer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Tiepolo" title="Giovanni Battista Tiepolo">Giovanni Battista Tiepolo</a> (5 March 1696 – 27 March 1770), the last "Grand Manner" fresco painter from the Venetian Republic.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tintoretto" title="Tintoretto">Tintoretto</a> (autumn 1518 – 31 May 1594), probably the last great painter of Italian Renaissance.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Titian" title="Titian">Titian</a> (<i>c.</i> 1488–90–27 August 1576), leader of the 16th-century Venetian school of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Renaissance" title="Italian Renaissance">Italian Renaissance</a> (he was born in <a href="/wiki/Cadore" title="Cadore">Pieve di Cadore</a>).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elisabetta_Camin%C3%A8r_Turra" title="Elisabetta Caminèr Turra">Elisabetta Caminèr Turra</a> (1751–1796), writer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Emilio_Vedova" title="Emilio Vedova">Emilio Vedova</a> (9 August 1919 – 25 October 2006), one of the most important modern painters of Italy.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sebastiano_Venier" title="Sebastiano Venier">Sebastiano Venier</a> (<i>c.</i> 1496–3 March 1578), <a href="/wiki/Doge_of_Venice" title="Doge of Venice">Doge of Venice</a> from 11 June 1577 to 1578.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Antonio_Vivaldi" title="Antonio Vivaldi">Antonio Vivaldi</a> (4 March 1678 – 28 [or 27] July 1741, <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>), composer and violinist of the Baroque Era.</li></ul>

<li id="cite_note-156"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-156">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Ranieri da Mosto, <i>Il Veneto in cucina</i>, Firenze, Aldo Martello-Giunti, 1974, p. 57; Mariù Salvatori de Zuliani, <i>A tola co i nostri veci. <li id="cite_note-157"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-157">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In other areas of Italy similar sweets are known by many other names, e.g. <i>cénci</i> (rags) (Florence), <i>frappe</i> (flounces) (Rome), <i>bugìe</i> (lies) (Turin, Genoa, etc.), <i>chiàcchiere</i> (chatter) (Milan and many other places in northern, central and southern Italy). Vid.: Pellegrino Artusi, <i>La Scienza in cucina e l'Arte di mangiar bene</i>, 93ª ristampa, Firenze, Giunti, 1960, p. 387, #595; Ranieri da Mosto, <i>Il Veneto in cucina</i>, Firenze, Aldo Martello-Giunti, 1974, p. 364; Luigi Veronelli (edited by), <i>Il Carnacina</i>, 10th ed., Milano, Garzanti, 1975, p. 656, #2013; to name but a few.</span>
</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bibliography">Bibliography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Bibliography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Venice#Bibliography" title="Timeline of Venice">Bibliography of the history of Venice</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic">Academic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Academic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047268">.mw-parser-output .refbegin{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul{list-style-type:none;margin-left:0}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul>li,.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>dl>dd{margin-left:0;padding-left:3.2em;text-indent:-3.2em;list-style:none}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-100{font-size:100%}</style><div class="refbegin columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul><li><cite class="citation book">Bosio, Luciano. <i>Le origini di Venezia</i>. Novara: Istituto Geografico De Agostini.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Le+origini+di+Venezia&amp;rft.place=Novara&amp;rft.pub=Istituto+Geografico+De+Agostini&amp;rft.aulast=Bosio&amp;rft.aufirst=Luciano&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AVenice" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Horatio_Brown" title="Horatio Brown">Brown, Horatio</a>, <i>Venice</i>, chapter 8 of <i><a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Modern_History" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge Modern History">Cambridge Modern History</a></i> vol. I <i>The Renaissance</i> (1902)</li>
<li>Brown, Horatio, <i>Calendar of State Papers (Venetian): 1581–1591</i>, 1895; <i>1592–1603</i>, 1897; <i>1603–1607</i>, 1900; <i>1607–1610</i>, 1904; <i>1610–1613</i>, 1905</li>
<li>Brown, Horatio, <i>Studies in the history of Venice</i> (London, 1907)</li>
<li>Chambers, D.S. (1970). <i>The Imperial Age of Venice, 1380–1580.</i> London: Thames &amp; Hudson. The best brief introduction in English, still completely reliable.</li>
<li>Contarini, Gasparo (1599). <i>The Commonwealth and Gouernment of Venice.</i> Lewes Lewkenor, trsl. London: "Imprinted by I. Windet for E. Mattes." The most important contemporary account of Venice's governance during the time of its blossoming. Also available in various reprint editions.</li>
<li>Da Canal, Martin, "Les estoires de Venise" (13th-century chronicle), translated by Laura Morreale. Padua, Unipress 2009.</li>
<li>Drechsler, Wolfgang (2002). "Venice Misappropriated." <i>Trames</i> 6(2), pp.&#160;192–201. A scathing review of Martin &amp; Romano 2000; also a good summary on the most recent economic and political thought on Venice.</li>
<li>Garrett, Martin, "Venice: a Cultural History" (2006). Revised edition of "Venice: a Cultural and Literary Companion" (2001).</li>
<li>Grubb, James S. (1986). "When Myths Lose Power: Four Decades of Venetian Historiography." <i>Journal of Modern History</i> 58, pp.&#160;43–94. The classic "muckraking" essay on the myths of Venice.</li>
<li>Lane, Frederic Chapin. <i>Venice: Maritime Republic</i> (1973) (<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-8018-1445-7" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-8018-1445-7">978-0-8018-1445-7</a>) standard scholarly history; emphasis on economic, political and diplomatic history</li>
<li>Laven, Mary, "Virgins of Venice: Enclosed Lives and Broken Vows in the Renaissance Convent (2002). The most important study of the life of Renaissance nuns, with much on aristocratic family networks and the life of women more generally.</li>
<li>Madden, Thomas F. <i>Enrico Dandolo and the Rise of Venice</i> Johns Hopkins University Press. Probably the best book in English on medieval Venice.</li>
<li>Martin, John Jeffries and Dennis Romano (eds). <i>Venice Reconsidered. The History and Civilization of an Italian City-State, 1297–1797.</i> (2002) <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University_Press" title="Johns Hopkins University Press">Johns Hopkins University Press</a>. The most recent collection on essays, many by prominent scholars, on Venice.</li>
<li>Muir, Edward (1981). <i>Civic Ritual in Renaissance Venice.</i> Princeton UP. The classic of Venetian cultural studies, highly sophisticated.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gerald_J._Oppenheimer" title="Gerald J. Oppenheimer">Oppenheimer, Gerald J.</a> (2010). <i>Venetian</i> Palazzi <i>and</i> Case: <i>A Guide to the Literature.</i> University of Washington, Seattle. Retrieved from <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110604034334/http://faculty.washington.edu/gerryo/venice.html">https://web.archive.org/web/20110604034334/http://faculty.washington.edu/gerryo/venice.html</a> 7 February 2010.</li>
<li>Rösch, Gerhard (2000). <i>Venedig. Geschichte einer Seerepublik.</i> Stuttgart: Kohlhammer. In German, but the most recent top-level brief history of Venice.</li>
<li><cite class="citation book">Miller, Judith (2005). <i>Furniture: world styles from classical to contemporary</i>. DK Publishing. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-7566-1340-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-7566-1340-2"><bdi>978-0-7566-1340-2</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Furniture%3A+world+styles+from+classical+to+contemporary&amp;rft.pub=DK+Publishing&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-7566-1340-2&amp;rft.aulast=Miller&amp;rft.aufirst=Judith&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AVenice" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></li></ul>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Popular">Popular</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Popular">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047268"/><div class="refbegin columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ackroyd,_Peter" class="mw-redirect" title="Ackroyd, Peter">Ackroyd, Peter</a>. <i>Venice: Pure City</i>. London, Chatto &amp; Windus. 2009. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-7011-8478-0" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-7011-8478-0">978-0-7011-8478-0</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Horatio_Brown" title="Horatio Brown">Brown, Horatio</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Life_on_the_Lagoons" title="Life on the Lagoons">Life on the Lagoons</a></i>, 1884; revised ed. 1894; further eds. 1900, 1904, 1909.</li>
<li>Cole, Toby. <i>Venice: A Portable Reader</i>, Lawrence Hill, 1979. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-88208-097-0" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-88208-097-0">978-0-88208-097-0</a> (hardcover); <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-88208-107-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-88208-107-6">978-0-88208-107-6</a> (softcover).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_F._Madden" title="Thomas F. Madden">Madden, Thomas</a>, <i>Venice: A New History</i>. New York: Viking, 2012. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-670-02542-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-670-02542-8">978-0-670-02542-8</a>. A fascinating and approachable history by a distinguished historian.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jan_Morris" title="Jan Morris">Morris, Jan</a> (1993), <i>Venice</i>. 3rd revised edition. Faber &amp; Faber, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-571-16897-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-571-16897-2">978-0-571-16897-2</a>. A subjective and passionate written introduction to the city and some of its history. Not illustrated.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Ruskin" title="John Ruskin">Ruskin, John (1853)</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Stones_of_Venice_(book)" title="The Stones of Venice (book)">The Stones of Venice</a></i>. Abridged edition Links, JG (Ed), Penguin Books, 2001. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-14-139065-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-14-139065-9">978-0-14-139065-9</a>. Seminal work on architecture and society</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andrea_di_Robilant" title="Andrea di Robilant">di Robilant, Andrea</a> (2004). <i>A Venetian Affair</i>. HarperCollins. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-84115-542-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-84115-542-5">978-1-84115-542-5</a> Biography of Venetian nobleman and lover, from correspondence in the 1750s.</li>
<li>Sethre, Janet. <i>The Souls of Venice</i> McFarland &amp; Company, Inc., 2003. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-7864-1573-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-7864-1573-1">978-0-7864-1573-1</a> (softcover). This book focuses on people who have been shaped by Venice and who have shaped the city in their turn. Illustrated (photographs by Manuela Fardin).</li></ul>
</div>
